The stores opening or expanding were Reinhold Jewelry, <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald\'s</a>, Adolfo Dominguez, and Cohen\'s Fashion Optical. <a href="/wiki/Church%27s_fried_chicken" class="mw-redirect" title="Church&#39;s fried chicken">Church\'s Fried Chicken</a> was under renovation, according to Vissepo. She explained that Reinhold was expanding to include space vacated by Thekes bookstore. After the expansion was complete, the jewelry store would occupy a total of 3,663 square feet. <a href="/wiki/McDonald%27s" title="McDonald&#39;s">McDonald\'s</a> new restaurant at the mall which required an investment of $1 million would occupy 3,123 square feet. "It will be located in the southern mall, between <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Borders_Book_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="Borders Book Store">Borders</a>," said Vissepo. Adolfo Dominguez, a Spanish fashion boutique, would occupy 1,194 square feet and would be located on the mall\'s first floor between <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a> and <a href="/wiki/JCPenney" title="JCPenney">J.C. Penney</a>. Meanwhile, Cohen\'s Fashion Optical would occupy the space previously used by women\'s apparel store Nostalgia; it measured 1,386 square feet.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2004, a former <a href="/wiki/Western_Auto" title="Western Auto">Western Auto</a> store on the premises of the mall was converted to a <a href="/wiki/Sears_Auto_Center" class="mw-redirect" title="Sears Auto Center">Sears Auto Center</a>.\n</p><p>In September 2005, the longstanding Plaza Theatres, which was by then operated by <a href="/wiki/CineVista_Theatres" title="CineVista Theatres">CineVista Theatres</a> would close.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On October 1, 2005, CV Entertainment Group, the owner company of <a href="/wiki/CineVista_Theatres" title="CineVista Theatres">CineVista Theatres</a>, announced an investment of US$6 million to transform the closed movie theater at the food court of Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas into a multimedia entertainment center that as of April 2006, would be known as Galaxy Lanes. It would include a mega bowling alley with 32 lanes, two restaurant areas, two bars (seating 500 people), 16 giant projection screens in the bowling area, a 20\'x20\' mega screen in the mezzanine area, multiple plasma monitors, wireless Internet connection, a dance floor and a DJ; a stage for live performances, pool tables, VIP rooms for parties, and a cabin for live radio and TV broadcasts. "We are talking about a 40,000 square-feet multimedia entertainment center," said CV Entertainment Group Marketing &amp; Operations VP Osvaldo Gonzalez.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 10, 2007, it was reported that Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, was in the midst of finalizing negotiations with <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> based retailer <a href="/wiki/Pottery_Barn" title="Pottery Barn">Pottery Barn</a> to open its first store on the island sometime in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 31, 2007, <a href="/wiki/Maxine_Clark" title="Maxine Clark">Maxine Clark</a>, founder and chief executive bear of <a href="/wiki/Build-A-Bear_Workshop" title="Build-A-Bear Workshop">Build-a-Bear</a>, announced the popular stuffed-animal chain had landed a coveted spot at Puerto Rico\'s premier shopping center, Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas. The Build-a-Bear store, which was under construction, was expected to open sometime late June to early July of that year featuring its collection of Build-a-Bear customized stuffed animals plus some customized items for the local market for a local flair. The store would be located on the mall\'s first floor, a couple of doors away from <a href="/wiki/Gap_Inc." title="Gap Inc.">The Gap</a>. In a market where there was practically no entertainment or educational  activities for children, \'tweens\' (ages 12-16) and for parents and children, Build-a-Bear was poised to become a bare necessity. The Plaza store was the first one of three to four locations expected to open on the island, each with a minimum investment of nearly $1 million and 35-40 full-time and part-time employees. "It was well worth the wait," said Clark during an exclusive interview, referring to the six-year wait to find the ideal location at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas. "I knew we wanted to be in the Puerto Rico market, but you have to start with the best location. Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas affords us the opportunity to truly showcase our concept and I\'m confident our family-oriented concept will win over the people of Puerto Rico. Island customers are warm and friendly people, very congruent with the in-store experience at Build-a-Bear."<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 10, 2008, it was reported that  <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> based <a href="/wiki/West_Elm" title="West Elm">West Elm</a> was set to begin operations at its first <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> store in Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas. During an exclusive interview, Dave DeMattei, president of west elm, confirmed, if successful, the Plaza store could be the first of several to open around the island. The store would have 20,000 square feet with 10,000 of those for selling space.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On March 5, 2009, it was reported that European giant retail beauty chain <a href="/wiki/Sephora" title="Sephora">Sephora</a>, which had revolutionized the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">U.S.</a> cosmetic market since 1998, was finally coming to <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>. Sephora representatives, who in the past had shown no interest in the local market, had been in conversations with Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas leasing management for awhile. The Puerto Rico store was part of the chain\'s multimillion dollar 2009 expansion plan. In 2001, there was an initial approach from the Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas team to Sephora, but to no avail; it was still too early in Sephora\'s mainland expansion plan. In 2008, during the annual ICSC (<a href="/wiki/International_Council_of_Shopping_Centers" title="International Council of Shopping Centers">International Council of Shopping Centers</a>) convention, it was confirmed Sephora had in fact accepted an invitation from  Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas to explore a scenario whereby the company would come to Puerto Rico. Still, Plaza officials kept a tight lid on the matter. But the wait was over. Construction of the first Sephora store was underway in the lower level at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, near <a href="/wiki/RadioShack" title="RadioShack">Radio Shack</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Elm" title="West Elm">West Elm</a>. To accommodate the beauty retailer, Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas had to relocate the former fast food corridor in that area to make room for the new store. The arrival of Sephora on the island, a brand that was already known by many <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Rican</a> customers who frequently traveled to the U.S. mainland, would certainly shake up the cosmetic and fragrance business category on the island, which was estimated to generate $100 million in annual sales.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 23, 2009, it was reported that Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas was preparing for the arrival of <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> based <a href="/wiki/Forever_21" title="Forever 21">Forever 21</a>, which would occupy the former Galaxy Lanes space in the mall\'s third level which had closed in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> store would be the chain\'s first in <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a>. Slated to open that summer. The multi-level 40,000 square foot Forever 21 location at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, adjacent to Plaza\'s La Terraza food court, was the latest flagship addition to the fashion chain with other international flagship operations in <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Korea" title="Korea">Korea</a>, <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">China</a> and <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>. It would generate 100 new jobs.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Expanding,_present_day:_2010s-2020s"><span id="Expanding.2C_present_day:_2010s-2020s"></span>Expanding, present day: 2010s-2020s</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Las_Am%C3%A9ricas_(Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Expanding, present day: 2010s-2020s"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<p>On June 9, 2011, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco</a> based furniture and home retailer <a href="/wiki/Pottery_Barn" title="Pottery Barn">Pottery Barn</a> (PB) likely would be closing its Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas store before  that year\'s end. Pottery Barn\'s exit, however, left space for the mall to relocate <a href="/wiki/Foot_Locker" title="Foot Locker">Foot Locker</a> to PB\'s 21,000 square foot location on the main level. Meanwhile, Foot Locker\'s space would be transformed into a much sexier store to be occupied by <a href="/wiki/Victoria%27s_Secret" title="Victoria&#39;s Secret">Victoria\'s Secret</a>, according to Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas sources.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On July 18, 2011, it was reported that after 40 years in business, giant book retailer <a href="/wiki/Borders_Group" title="Borders Group">Borders Group</a> would exit the market entirely and sell off its entire inventory. <a href="/wiki/Borders_Group" title="Borders Group">Borders</a> filed for Chapter 11 of the Bankruptcy Law in February of that year and in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a> announced that same month the closure of its stores in <a href="/wiki/Carolina,_Puerto_Rico" title="Carolina, Puerto Rico">Carolina</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez,_Puerto_Rico" title="Mayag\xc3\xbcez, Puerto Rico">Mayag\xc3\xbcez</a>, and the subsequent liquidation. The Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas store was also reported to be closing its doors.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In January 2012, it was reported that Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas had retained control of the former <a href="/wiki/Borders_Book_Store" class="mw-redirect" title="Borders Book Store">Borders</a> space. The mall was now in a position to negotiate a future rental agreement of the 34,000 square-foot prime location.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> \n</p><p>On October 7, 2011, the magical world of the <a href="/wiki/Disney_Store" title="Disney Store">Disney Stores</a> returned to the Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas shopping center after having closed its doors several years earlier. Dozens of eager people gathered at the mall to be the first to enjoy the store that was inaugurated that day. Boxer <a href="/wiki/Tito_Trinidad" class="mw-redirect" title="Tito Trinidad">Tito Trinidad</a>, along with his family, was in charge of opening the store.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 23, 2012, it was reported that Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas invested $12 million in remodeling the mall\'s north entrance facade. The remodeling work began on May 23, 2012, and was completed by mid November 2012, just before the holiday season. In addition, between July\xe2\x80\x93August 2012, expansion began on the multistory parking, located in the southern area of the mall. The expansion extended the five floors of multistory to add over 300 parking spaces. All parking areas of the mall were also repaved while new landscape gardens designs where developed in front of the main entrance.<sup id="cite_ref-plaza2012_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-plaza2012-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> \n</p><p>On December 18, 2012, Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas confirmed that it signed an agreement for the establishment of <a href="/wiki/The_Cheesecake_Factory" title="The Cheesecake Factory">The Cheesecake Factory</a> in the shopping center. The establishment would have approximately 10,000 square feet and be located next to the new entrance, near Avenida Chard\xc3\xb3n. Construction of the restaurant was expected to begin in early 2013 and would open its doors to the public during the third quarter of the year. The investment was estimated at around $8 million.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 28, 2013, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Karen_Millen" title="Karen Millen">Karen Millen</a> would be opening their first store in Puerto Rico at the mall. Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas would also usher in its first <a href="/wiki/Starbucks_Coffee" class="mw-redirect" title="Starbucks Coffee">Starbucks Coffee</a> shop in the following months, to be located in a 943 square foot space between <a href="/wiki/JCPenney" title="JCPenney">JCPenney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On April 4, 2014, <a href="/wiki/Sports_Authority" title="Sports Authority">Sports Authority</a> would open a store at Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> It would later on close in March 2016 due to the chains bankruptcy.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 16, 2016, it would be reported that new stores would arrive at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas with the announcement of the opening of Zapaventura, BienLatino, a second <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> store and <a href="/wiki/Olive_Garden" title="Olive Garden">Olive Garden</a>. Zapaventura would open in the following weeks, while BienLatino and Starbucks were scheduled to open in August and September of that year, respectively. In the case of <a href="/wiki/Olive_Garden" title="Olive Garden">Olive Garden</a>, construction would begin in the middle of the year and the opening was scheduled for the first quarter of 2017. Zapaventura, chaired by the former general manager of the Chiquit\xc3\xadn stores, would open in the same place that the popular chain of quality children\'s footwear formerly occupied. They would sell the same shoe lines that were previously offered. Bienlatino, specializing in sandwiches, soups and salads, would open in a space of more than 2,100 square feet, in front of <a href="/wiki/Applebee%27s" title="Applebee&#39;s">Applebees</a>, on the first level of the south corridor. The new <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> store, of approximately 1,500 square feet, would be located in front of the North fountain, right next to the Banco <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bank" title="Santander Bank">Santander</a> branch and <a href="/wiki/Olive_Garden" title="Olive Garden">Olive Garden</a>, of approximately 7,700 square feet, would be on the third level of the Central Atrium, in front of the Restaurant Land of Fire. Franklin Domenech, General Manager at the time of Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, pointed out that "the most visible remodeling works of Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas concluded last year with the restoration of the skylight of the north fountain and the north panoramic elevator, the facade of La Terraza and the connecting corridor between The Terrace and the third level of the Central Atrium, where <a href="/wiki/Walgreens" title="Walgreens">Walgreens</a> is. Now we are remodeling the elevators of La Torre de PLAZA and soon the remodeling of the area in front of Banco <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bank" title="Santander Bank">Santander</a> and <a href="/wiki/Red_Lobster" title="Red Lobster">Red Lobster</a> will begin," he concluded. Rafael Ruiz-Comas, Director of Corporate Leasing added that "this year the Tiffany and A\'gaci stores have already opened and we expect more activity in new stores during the second half of 2016 to continue strengthening our commercial offer, starting with these four new stores that we are announcing today and that are owned by <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Ricans" title="Puerto Ricans">Puerto Rican</a> businessmen and investors". Mr. Ruiz Comas also informed that in the hallway where Banco <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bank" title="Santander Bank">Santander</a> was located, first level near the North fountain, a transformation would soon begin with the start of construction of the first <a href="/wiki/Red_Lobster" title="Red Lobster">Red Lobster</a> in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, the construction of <a href="/wiki/Starbucks" title="Starbucks">Starbucks</a> and the expansion of the Playero store and the <a href="/wiki/Pearle_Opticians" class="mw-redirect" title="Pearle Opticians">Pearle optician</a>. <a href="/wiki/Red_Lobster" title="Red Lobster">Red Lobster</a> would occupy approximately 8,000 square feet of space where the Banco <a href="/wiki/Santander_Bank" title="Santander Bank">Santander</a> branch was previously located. Playero increased its space to occupy 2,500 square feet, including the corner where the Lugano Jewelry store used to be. Lugano, for its part, was relocated to the second level of the Central Atrium, in front of the Bose store. <a href="/wiki/Pearle_Vision" title="Pearle Vision">Pearle Vision</a> would occupy a space of more than 3,000 square feet, between the Playero and <a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> stores. During the construction of Playero and Pearle, both stores would continue to operate in temporary locations as opposed to their permanent spaces and the new stores were expected to be ready by the last quarter of this year. <a href="/wiki/Red_Lobster" title="Red Lobster">Red Lobster</a> would begin construction in the third quarter of the year and it was expected to start operations in April 2017. Other changes that would be happening in the shopping center were the relocation of the Galer\xc3\xada shoe store, which moved to the corridor between <a href="/wiki/JCPenney" title="JCPenney">JCPenney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a>, in front of the <a href="/wiki/Guess_(company)" title="Guess (company)">Guess</a> store, and the remodeling and expansion of <a href="/wiki/Sizzler" title="Sizzler">Sizzler</a>, in the La Terraza area.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 27, 2017, it would be reported that after 12 years in Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, <a href="/wiki/Brooks_Brothers" title="Brooks Brothers">Brooks Brothers</a> would close its boutique located in the central corridor of the shopping center, to receive a new tenant.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On February 22, 2018, taking over the 34,000 square foot space left by <a href="/wiki/Sports_Authority" title="Sports Authority">Sports Authority</a>. A new <a href="/wiki/Marshalls" title="Marshalls">Marshalls</a> store would open at Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2018, the mall celebrated its 50th anniversary.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 17, 2019, <a href="/wiki/Jaime_Fonalledas" title="Jaime Fonalledas">Empresas Fonalledas</a> announced that <a href="/wiki/Burlington_(department_store)" title="Burlington (department store)">Burlington</a> would occupy the space left by the <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title="Toys &quot;R&quot; Us">Toy \'R\' Us</a> toy store in Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, and that the opening was planned for that fall season.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On December 25, 2019, it was announced that Cuba Libre Restaurant and Rum Bar will be constructed in the mall, originally set to open by January 2021,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> but due to economic loss caused by the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, this project was delayed. In February 2021, despite delays, the chain stated that the restaurant would still be built;<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> however, in June 2022, the project was ultimately canceled.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2020, the mall closed until further notice due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. Following the. announcement of a new executive order on May 21, the mall reopened on June 1 with security measures, including new hours, mandatory face masks and social distancing. Reservations were now required to visit the mall and were originally limited to 2 people. On June 9, reservations were changed to allow up to 4 people. On July 1, it was announced that the reservations would no longer be required to visit the mall starting July 3, though face masks were still a mandatory requirement. The mask requirement were dropped in March 2022 following new government regulations.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 25, 2021, it would be reported that the <a href="/wiki/Toys_%22R%22_Us" title="Toys &quot;R&quot; Us">Toys "R" Us</a> chain said it would open its stores within the <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a> Department Store and that its <a href="/wiki/Flagship#Retailing" title="Flagship">flagship</a> store would be at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 21, 2021, it would reported that both remaining <a href="/wiki/Disney_Store" title="Disney Store">Disney Stores</a> on the island would close, which included the Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas store. They were to close before June 16 of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On November 8, 2021, it was reported that <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a> Backstage would be taking over the second floor of the former <a href="/wiki/Borders_Group" title="Borders Group">Borders Books</a> and that it would be opening by November 20.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On August 17, 2022,  Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas announced the opening of new stores, including the well known Colombian brand V\xc3\xa9lez, specializing in handmade leather and fur items, and the clothing and accessories chain Windsor Fashion. During the month of September, the <a href="/wiki/Arby%27s" title="Arby&#39;s">Arby\'s</a> restaurant was expected to open in the La Terraza area. In addition, the reopening of <a href="/wiki/Michael_Kors" title="Michael Kors">Michael Kors</a> was expected on the first level of the central atrium. For October it would be up to Windsor Fashion. The store would be located on the second level in front of the north fountain escalators, in a space of about 6,300 square feet.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On October 15, 2022, it was announced that the <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a> store, the last in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, would be closed by the end of that month.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On January 30, 2023, a 42,000 square foot <a href="/wiki/Dave_%26_Buster%27s" title="Dave &amp; Buster&#39;s">Dave &amp; Buster\'s</a> would open at Plaza las Am\xc3\xa9ricas on the third level of the mall.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On May 8, 2023, the <a href="/wiki/Red_Lobster" title="Red Lobster">Red Lobster</a> in Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, the only restaurant of that chain that remained open in <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, closed its doors for good, and was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Longhorn_Steakhouse" class="mw-redirect" title="Longhorn Steakhouse">Longhorn Steakhouse</a> in May 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>On June 15, 2023, Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas announced the arrival of new stores that have already opened or will be opening in time for the summer season,  complementing the current offerings in fashion and gastronomy. Retailer Liage had already opened on the second level of Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas, next to <a href="/wiki/T-Mobile_US" title="T-Mobile US">T-Mobile</a> and opposite the north fountain. Occupying approximately 900 square feet, Liage offers an exclusive selection of products for facial, skin and hair care for both women and men. Likewise, Cake by Glorimar, known for its cakes and sweets, had also arrived at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas. The kiosk is located opposite Chico\'s on the shopping mall\'s first level and promises to delight visitors with its desserts and customized options. In early July, APM Monaco was set to open around 900 square feet of retail space next to Euromoda Sport on the mall\'s first level. At the end of July, Studio F, a Colombian fashion brand, was expected to open on the first level of the mall, adjacent to Modernica. Occupying approximately 3,300 square feet, Studio F will offer a wide array of elegant and modern clothing and accessories for men and women. Meanwhile, international fashion brand <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> has completed the expansion of its space at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas on the first level, situated between Clark\'s and La Favorita stores. It now spans more than 34,000 square feet, combining the original <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> space with the area previously occupied by <a href="/wiki/Gap_Inc." title="Gap Inc.">Gap</a>. This 12,000 square-foot expansion would provide customers with a more diverse shopping experience, including <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> Kids and <a href="/wiki/Zara_(retailer)" title="Zara (retailer)">Zara</a> Man, in addition to the women\'s section, Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas officials said. Moreover, Urban Beauty, which offers a selection of hair care products and tools, has relocated in front of the <a href="/wiki/Carolina_Herrera" title="Carolina Herrera">Carolina Herrera</a> store on the second level, between <a href="/wiki/JCPenney" title="JCPenney">JCPenney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a>. The new Urban Beauty space covers approximately 1,900 square feet. Lastly, in August, Preciosa would relocate to the second level to the approximately 1,600-square-foot space currently occupied by Mundo Mattress, to make way for the construction of Bimba y Lola, which would cover approximately 2,000 square feet. Bimba y Lola is a Spanish fashion brand that offers affordable designer clothing and accessories for women. Meanwhile, Mundo Mattress will relocate to the second level into the space previously occupied by Beauty Factory, covering approximately 1,100 square feet. Also, La Patisserie de France would relocate in front of Soft &amp; Creamy on the first level, occupying approximately 2,800 square feet.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2024, <a href="/wiki/Chili%27s_Grill_%26_Bar" class="mw-redirect" title="Chili&#39;s Grill &amp; Bar">Chili\'s Grill &amp; Bar</a> would announce they would remodel their location at the mall.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Notable_attributes">Notable attributes</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Las_Am%C3%A9ricas_(Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notable attributes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<figure class="mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Plaza_Las_Americas_Entrance.JPG" Caribbean Cinemas and mall entrance on the second floor</figcaption></figure>\n<ul><li>It is the largest shopping center in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Plaza\'s <a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a> was the first one to open in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-auto_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-auto-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>Plaza\'s <a href="/wiki/Chili%27s" title="Chili&#39;s">Chili\'s</a> is the highest grossing in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>It has the world\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Romano%27s_Macaroni_Grill" title="Romano&#39;s Macaroni Grill">Romano\'s Macaroni Grill</a> restaurant.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li>It houses the first <a href="/wiki/The_Cheesecake_Factory" title="The Cheesecake Factory">Cheesecake Factory</a> restaurant in the Caribbean, officially opened on August 28, 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sports_Authority" title="Sports Authority">Sports Authority</a> became the sixth largest anchor store, first opened up in mid-2014, followed by an expansion of parking spaces. It closed in 2016 after the company declared bankruptcy and was replaced by a <a href="/wiki/Marshalls" title="Marshalls">Marshalls</a> in February 2018.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Dave_%26_Buster%27s" title="Dave &amp; Buster&#39;s">Dave &amp; Buster\'s</a> opened at the mall on January 30, 2023, right across from <a href="/wiki/Olive_Garden" title="Olive Garden">Olive Garden</a> on the third floor.</li>\n<li>Notable former stores at Plaza Las Am\xc3\xa9ricas are <a href="/wiki/Kmart" title="Kmart">Kmart</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pottery_Barn" title="Pottery Barn">Pottery Barn</a>, <a href="/wiki/KB_Toys" title="KB Toys">KB Toys</a>, <a href="/wiki/RadioShack" title="RadioShack">RadioShack</a>, <a href="/wiki/GameStop" title="GameStop">GameStop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Borders_Bookstores" class="mw-redirect" title="Borders Bookstores">Borders Bookstores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gap,_Inc." class="mw-redirect" title="Gap, Inc.">GAP</a>.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a> became the last location in Puerto Rico that remains currently active in this mall after all other outlets were closed down.</li></ul>\n<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Current_anchor_stores">Current anchor stores</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Plaza_Las_Am%C3%A9ricas_(Puerto_Rico)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Current anchor stores"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/JCPenney" title="JCPenney">JCPenney</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Macy%27s" title="Macy&#39;s">Macy\'s</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sears" title="Sears">Sears</a></li>\n<li>Sears Brand Central &amp;
